  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2f8ffeb3-618f-4b09-a6f6-613dab14d2c0'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText7059286474045882262" style="display:none">Too much time has passed since the powerful dragon Tintaglia helped the people of the Trader cities stave off an invasion of their enemies. The Traders have forgotten their promises, weary of the labor and expense of tending earthbound dragons who were hatched weak and deformed by a river turned toxic. If neglected, the creatures will rampage--or die--so it is decreed that they must move farther upriver toward Kelsingra, the mythical homeland whose location is locked deep within the dragons' uncertain ancestral memories.<br /><br />Thymara, an unschooled forest girl, and Alise, wife of an unloving and wealthy Trader, are among the disparate group entrusted with escorting the dragons to their new home. And on an extraordinary odyssey with no promise of return, many lessons will be learned--as dragons and tenders alike experience hardships, betrayals . . . and joys beyond their wildest imaginings.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The cool thing about Hobb's books is they are structured as stand-alone trilogies (exception: Rain Wild Chronicles and its quadrilogy) but if you deci<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The cool thing about Hobb's books is they are structured as stand-alone trilogies (exception: Rain Wild Chronicles and its quadrilogy) but if you decide to read them from the beginning and in order, a lot of nuances you would otherwise have missed come into focus.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1830297194" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3316512113105438684"><b>3.5/5 stars<br/><br/>A good foundational start to a quartet but it’s also the weakest start within any of Hobb's series so far.</b><br/><br/>Dragon Keeper is the first book in the Rain Wild Chronicles quartet, which also marks the beginning of the fourth out of five subseries within Hobb’s The Realm of the Elderlings series. The entire storyline in this book took place in the Rain Wild section of the world and plot-wise, the first book has a very simple premise. The Dragon Keepers have to herd the dragons to find their</span>
  <span id="freeText3316512113105438684" style="display:none"><b>3.5/5 stars<br /><br />A good foundational start to a quartet but it’s also the weakest start within any of Hobb's series so far.</b><br /><br />Dragon Keeper is the first book in the Rain Wild Chronicles quartet, which also marks the beginning of the fourth out of five subseries within Hobb’s The Realm of the Elderlings series. The entire storyline in this book took place in the Rain Wild section of the world and plot-wise, the first book has a very simple premise. The Dragon Keepers have to herd the dragons to find their lost legendary city, Kelsingra. That’s it, that’s seriously the plot of this book. There’s no complexity in the story so far, it’s completely a setup for the next three books. There are no climax sequences or tense moments, completely zero actions here; even less than all Hobb’s previous books. The climax sequences—if you can call it that—revolves around the Dragon Keepers fighting over an Elk’s meat to share. Yup, you heard that right. Fighting over an Elk’s meat. Bloody intense, bruh, I’m shaking in my boots. I’m not sure but I heard this is the publisher’s fault as this was supposed to be one giant book but the publisher decided to divide it into two instead and it makes the book to not have any sense of ending.<br /><br />We follow the story from the perspective of five new characters: Thymara, Alise, Sedric, Leftrin, and Sintara. As I said before, this is just a foundational book. Although it’s almost 600 pages long, almost nothing actually happened in the story, it’s all about laying the groundwork for future books by doing characterizations first. The characterizations were great but I’m still not charmed by them like how I was with Fitz or the characters in the Liveship Traders. The problem is I felt the characters felt a bit too childish or YA-ish, even the way Hobb wrote them felt different to Hobb’s usual complex characters. Plus, the dragon’s POV was boring. I’m a fan of Hobb’s Liveship Traders trilogy but even there, one of my minor complaints were the Serpent’s PO; the Dragon’s POV was practically the same thing as that. If you enjoyed the Serpent’s POV in Liveship Traders you might not face this problem.<br /><br />The main highlight of this book for me was the Liveship Traders characters cameo. They didn’t appear a lot but when they do, I was overjoyed but their appearance, Hobb has written something really great about her characters in the Liveship Traders in my opinion.<br /><br />Hobb’s prose here also felt a bit different. It still captivated me and the characterizations were great, but it’s simply not as great compared to how she wrote Farseer, Liveship Traders or Tawny Man trilogy. I usually end up highlighting a lot of passages/quotes in her books, there’s absolutely none here which I found memorable.<br /><br />Overall, Dragon Keeper is a good foundational book but it’s certainly Hobb’s weakest start in her gigantic series. However, I’m hopeful that the foundation laid here will bring a great result for the next three books in this quartet.<br /><br /><i>You can find <b><a href="http://booknest.eu/reviews/pat/1080-dragonkeeper" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a></b> and the rest of my Adult Epic/High Fantasy &amp; Sci-Fi reviews at <b><a href="http://booknest.eu/review/patrick" rel="nofollow noopener">BookNest</a></b></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="3316512113105438684" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_91314153" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/91314153" />
    <a title="else fine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/83476-else-fine"><img alt="else fine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1179006794p2/83476.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/91314153?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="else fine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="else fine" href="/user/show/83476-else-fine">else fine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061561627" href="/book/show/6550760-dragon-keeper">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83476-else-fine?shelf=read2010">read2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83476-else-fine?shelf=sf-fantasy-general">sf-fantasy-general</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer91314153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15920521473249846268">I grew up on a toxic waste dump. I realize that sounds melodramatic, but technically it's accurate. My childhood home was ringed by no fewer than five Superfund sites - and, as we like to say, those are just the spots they've <i>cleaned</i>. <br/><br/>When I was a kid people weren't so concerned about the pollution. Arsenic was in the dust we kicked up on the playgrounds, on the berries we picked in the woods, in the small ponds where nothing lived and no birds ever stopped. The waterways were lined with gray he</span>
  <span id="freeText15920521473249846268" style="display:none">I grew up on a toxic waste dump. I realize that sounds melodramatic, but technically it's accurate. My childhood home was ringed by no fewer than five Superfund sites - and, as we like to say, those are just the spots they've <i>cleaned</i>. <br /><br />When I was a kid people weren't so concerned about the pollution. Arsenic was in the dust we kicked up on the playgrounds, on the berries we picked in the woods, in the small ponds where nothing lived and no birds ever stopped. The waterways were lined with gray heaps of slag from the copper smelter, in some spots enlivened by oil-slick rainbow stains made by unknown chemicals seeping out from the rocks. We were told not to fish or swim in the bay, which seemed to us kids to be hilarious: looking down off the docks into the still, metallic depths, we couldn't picture fish living down there at all, let alone anything you'd think of eating. And that was just the water. I still don't know what the mills were belching into the air, or what they're still churning out - sometimes, when the wind is right, you can both smell and taste the air: a sulphuric grit which stings your eyes and irritates your throat. <br /><br />Now it's been spruced up. They sealed off the slag heaps and built fancy condos on top of them, planted new grass along the edges, dug up people's lawns and replaced them with new, cleaner topsoil. The smelter company offered a cash settlement to the people living closest to the plant, and they took it, even though the surveys hadn't been completed. They worked hard to restore the bay, and now when you stroll through the new grass and out along the docks you can look down to see bright colonies of starfish and sea anemones clinging to the piers, and deeper down, the quick dark shapes of fish.<br /><br />Later, of course, we learned that the pollution went farther and deeper than the smelter operators had admitted to. Too late for the people who had settled, and too late for all of us who grew up splashing in that water and breathing that air. Statistics are readily available about disease rates in my hometown, telling us that you're much more likely to die of obscure cancers or get heart or lung disease there. I haven't seen anything on autoimmune disease, except that it's a hotspot for diabetes. I'm curious mostly because everyone I know, just about, has something crazy and unlikely wrong with them. Lupus, MS, celiac disease, autism, Crohn's disease, asthma - you name it. We're a sickly bunch. <br /><br />We're not alone. All over the planet, people grow up in the shadow of industrial toxins, watch their kids and their friends get sick and die, watch their own bodies with wary concern. What can you do? You go on. Sometimes your pain and your poison can be transmuted into something beautiful, into art, into action, into something meaningful. Sometimes you just have to learn to accept your limitations and endure the pain.<br /><br />And so this is a story for us. Here is a world where profit has trumped issues of morality and health, where generations grow up living with the legacy of pollution. It's sort of a counterpoint to the sunny ending of the Liveship books, where dragons and men are reunited and the deformed people of the Rain Wilds are transformed into something better. In this new series, we meet the people who were left behind, still deformed, without the hope that some magical intervention will save them from themselves. How they go on, and how they learn to transform themselves, is nothing short of inspirational. <br /><br />This is what fantasy is best at, and this is why it's necessary.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15920521473249846268" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1253867345" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1253867345" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1253867345?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=4-star-reads">4-star-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1253867345" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18364817438755141917">I feel somewhat sorry for the dragons in this. They spent the entirety of the Liveship Trader’s trilogy trying to find a place to evolve out of their basic serpent form, and when they do find it most of them die in the process. They’re too mutated and twisted to be able to develop into dragons. Only fourteen remain by the end and even those are stunted and unusual, that much so that the dragon Tintaglia abandons them for a richer prospect, mating with the ancient dragon Icefyre in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45108.Fool_s_Fate' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fool's Fate</a>. S</span>
  <span id="freeText18364817438755141917" style="display:none">I feel somewhat sorry for the dragons in this. They spent the entirety of the Liveship Trader’s trilogy trying to find a place to evolve out of their basic serpent form, and when they do find it most of them die in the process. They’re too mutated and twisted to be able to develop into dragons. Only fourteen remain by the end and even those are stunted and unusual, that much so that the dragon Tintaglia abandons them for a richer prospect, mating with the ancient dragon Icefyre in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45108.Fool_s_Fate" rel="nofollow noopener">Fool's Fate</a>. So they're on their own. <br /><br /><b> Nobody wants them </b><br /><br />These new dragons are a nuisance. The Rain Wild folk want them gone because they are a blight on their recourses; they want them gone because they are growing increasingly dangerous and are wanting more and more food as they get even bigger. In addition, some mutated teenagers amongst their own people are a so called embarrassment to civilisation. So, ever so pragmatically, the rulers decide to pair up one of these weird kids with a dragon and send them off on their own looking for an ancient city. Sounds like a great move? They lose two problems, but don’t really consider the consequence of possible success. <br /><br />Thymara has been hated all her life for her lizard features; thus, when a chance like this comes up she jumps at it, and who can blame her. Not many people get to interact with dragons albeit stunted ones. Her dragon, however, is haughty and superior; she distains all those she perceives as beneath her. So Tymara has a rather interesting task on her hands, which leads to some difficult and amusing situations. She has to deal with a dragon who thinks herself a god of the sky when in reality she is half grown and misshapen, and is struggling to accept the realities of who she is. It seems to me these two are perfectly suited to each other. <br /><br /><b> They are driven by ancient memories </b><br /><br />I love the complexities of the dragons here. They remember all the lives of their ancestors, and they consume the bodies of dead dragons to gain more memories. This way the dragons are wise and experienced without having to do anything to get such gifts. This means that these dragons, though young, know exactly how to salvage their situation and grow into their destinies as rulers of the sky. They are instinctively driven to the ancient city of Kelsingra; their refuge and new beginning. <br /><br />So this drives the novel forward, and gives the characters hope in an almost impossibly difficult situation. But, this is a Robin Hobb novel. So that means the story is paced out superbly with the journey only beginning as the book closes. She really knows how to add such depth to her world. From this point, I think this series has more potential than the LiveShip Traders. The story seems tighter and the characters more desperate. There’s going to be some exciting times ahead reading the reading the next three books; it has been far too long Robin Hobb, the queen of fantasy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18364817438755141917" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_172716864" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/172716864" />
    <a title="Felicia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/666892-felicia"><img alt="Felicia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437521850p2/666892.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/172716864?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Felicia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Felicia" href="/user/show/666892-felicia">Felicia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666892-felicia?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer172716864" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8776824698796303505">Robin Hobb wrote a few of my FAVORITE series, Assassin's Apprentice and the Liveship Traders, so I'm always a fan of her books. This one was as well written as the others, but it felt slow to start, and as soon as the story picked up, the book ended! JUST AS I GOT INTO IT!<br/><br/>So, I guess I should be waiting for the next book excitedly to continue the story, but considering the subject matter of the book, I'm a bit reluctant to follow up with the series, for totally squeamish personal reasons. The wh</span>
  <span id="freeText8776824698796303505" style="display:none">Robin Hobb wrote a few of my FAVORITE series, Assassin's Apprentice and the Liveship Traders, so I'm always a fan of her books. This one was as well written as the others, but it felt slow to start, and as soon as the story picked up, the book ended! JUST AS I GOT INTO IT!<br /><br />So, I guess I should be waiting for the next book excitedly to continue the story, but considering the subject matter of the book, I'm a bit reluctant to follow up with the series, for totally squeamish personal reasons. The whole story follows dragons, MALFORMED dragons who can't really take care of themselves. I am a person who's favorite movie is Babe. Yeah, the pig movie. While at the movies watching the Peter Jackson King Kong redo, I became so hysterical when they were capturing the ape that I had to leave the theatre and NOT GO BACK IN. Ever. Yeah, so I'm kind of irrational when reading about animals in danger, or even threatened. So basically, the set up for the next books is gonna lead to a LOT OF DRAGON TRAUMA, I JUST KNOW IT! And I dunno if I can personally hang in there. Robin Hobb is great at torturing her characters, and I'm cool with doing that to humans, but doing it to the dragons may not be something I can sign up for, ultimate happy ending or not.<br /><br />I know this review doesn't help anyone, haha, but whatever. That's the deal. The book was slow to start but ok, and I'm sure it will continue wonderfully. For those who aren't a little bit crazy :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="8776824698796303505" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3032869090" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3032869090" />
    <a title="Deborah Obida" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida"><img alt="Deborah Obida" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604679377p2/54790180.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3032869090?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deborah Obida" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deborah Obida" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida">Deborah Obida</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8176880-dragon-keeper">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3032869090" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3503196235800254385">Dragon Keeper is the first book in The Rain Wilds Chronicles and the fourth sub series in Hobb's Realm of the Elderlings series.<br/><br/>Though I enjoyed reading this book I have to admit that this is her weakest book. If you are familiar with Robin Hobb you will know that her books focus more on character development than plot progression, this book is different, the book aspects are extremely slow, it was fun to read that's why I still rated it high.<br/><br/>This book took place some years after <i>Liveship Trader</i></span>
  <span id="freeText3503196235800254385" style="display:none">Dragon Keeper is the first book in The Rain Wilds Chronicles and the fourth sub series in Hobb's Realm of the Elderlings series.<br /><br />Though I enjoyed reading this book I have to admit that this is her weakest book. If you are familiar with Robin Hobb you will know that her books focus more on character development than plot progression, this book is different, the book aspects are extremely slow, it was fun to read that's why I still rated it high.<br /><br />This book took place some years after <i>Liveship Traders</i> in the infamous Rain Wilds. Life there is harder than I thought when I read Liveship. The Khurprus family is rich so I didn't feel it much. The middle-class and those below struggle to make end meet.<br /><br />Dragon Keeper is about the serpents that went to cacoon at the end of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45102.Ship_of_Destiny__Liveship_Traders___3_" title="Ship of Destiny (Liveship Traders, #3) by Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Ship of Destiny</a>, instead of the dragon to be as magnificent as Tintaglia they were crippled and none could fly so that means they can not hunt, they have to be feed. The traders got tired of feeding them after five years and decided to send them off to another location with some misfits for keepers.<br /><br />Thymara, Tats and Rapskal were some of those misfits. Thymara and Rapskal are both rain wilders and badly marked while Tats is a former slave. All three are teenagers. Thymara is naive and insecure, she's a good person but have a long way to go. She also have a POV which ia fun to read sometimes.<br /><br />Elise is a Bingtown woman who have been obsessed with dragons, she has studied them for a ling time in old scrolls. She decided to escape her bad marriage by going after her dream of studying dragons. Her POV is fun to read, I'm loving her character development.<br /><br />Sedic is a gray character, he is selfish but can be kind occasionally.<br /><br />Leftrin is another character with a POV, he's POV isn't that engaging but it's okay.<br /><br />Sintara is the only dragon with a POV, despite been a cripple she is arrogant, selfish and self centred, she cares for no one but herself.<br /><br />The writing and world building is definitely above average, The plot is focusing too much on the romantic life of the characters that it's making this book look like a slow burn romance. The book is written in third person multiple POV of the aforementioned characters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3503196235800254385" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1327238448" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1327238448" />
    <a title="Kaitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin"><img alt="Kaitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481663259p2/19126246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1327238448?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlin" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin">Kaitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1327238448" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12811059923801634055">I read this book once again as a buddy read with my loyal group of Robin Hobb readers. We're all a bit obsessed with her work by this point honestly and we'd all been missing this world and these characters so being able to dive back into a story of Elderlings, Magic, Monsters and Myths was just wonderful and although this isn't my favourite of her books I still really enjoyed this. It is a shorter book than many of the Hobb ones I've recently read, and the story does have a few skips in time an</span>
  <span id="freeText12811059923801634055" style="display:none">I read this book once again as a buddy read with my loyal group of Robin Hobb readers. We're all a bit obsessed with her work by this point honestly and we'd all been missing this world and these characters so being able to dive back into a story of Elderlings, Magic, Monsters and Myths was just wonderful and although this isn't my favourite of her books I still really enjoyed this. It is a shorter book than many of the Hobb ones I've recently read, and the story does have a few skips in time and a little bit of recapping which I didn't love, but honestly it's Robin Hobb and her excellent world and characters and we do see some truly wonderful developments in this book.<br /><br />This book in particular is set in the Rain Wilds, a section which we have already explored a little in the Liveship Traders books and it's a place which I instantly fell in love with. The people of the Rain Wilds have to live in vast, enormous canopies of trees because the river that they live near is toxic and erodes boats and skin alike. The only boats that can travel the river are the Liveships which have magical properties, and the people who live in the area suffer greatly for their proximity to the river and harsh land. However, there are many secrets and adventures to be found here too and we follow a couple of new characters in this book who promise to discover to some pretty big events and secrets. <br /><br />The characters who are new in this book include Captain Leftrin, Thymara and Alise. Each of these characters lives either within Bingtown, the Rain Wilds or is a trader with the two and has a lot of ties to both these places and the people we've met in previous books who live here too. I found myself quickly being intrigued by each of them, although I think that Thymara and Alise were easily the two whom I connected with quickest. I enjoyed Leftrin's story too, it just took me a little while to warm up to him.<br />Leftrin is a trader who uses his ship, the oldest one which can travel the Rain Wild River, to trade up and down it. He's a middle aged fellow with few prospects ahead other than his day to day life which he enjoys immensely...until he meets someone and his whole perspective is changed and challenged and his view of day to day life gets manipulated too. I liked Leftrin as a character the more I got to know him but he does still feel like the character we know the least about. He's a likeable person with some unlucky situations, I will certainly look out for more of him in the upcoming books!<br />Thymara is a young girl who was never meant to be alive. She's a disgrace, a monster and even her own family (except her father) wanted to dispose of her. I instantly liked her spark of life and her adventurous and intelligent nature. Being constantly known as an outsider she's someone I found interesting to read about and her story quickly takes some very exciting turns which I have no doubt will lead to more and more adventure!<br />Finally Alise, she's probably the one we most focus on in this book and she's certainly someone who I liked and then didn't like and then liked. I liked her because she's an expert on Dragons and Elderlings which is something I too have a fascination with. She's calm and clever and full of ideas of what she wants to do, she's also a little weak and doesn't quite have that spark that we know some of Hobbs other characters have found or developed. Over the course of the book we do see the beginnings of her finding herself, and I found that by the ending I was really loving who she was becoming :)<br />We do have some other characters too such as Tats, Sedric and Hest, all of whom are also new and very different. Some of them are sweet and kind, others mean and horrible. I love that Hobb can really make me feel strong emotions of all kinds towards her characters and for each of these three my feelings were ever tested.<br /><br />As for the pacing of this book it was a little bit rushed at times. I've become used to seeing a slow build up with Robin Hobb towards an eventual epic conclusion and parts of this book did skip forwards through large chunks in order to tell a story more completely. Whilst I liked that we got to the present day storyline, I felt it could maybe have been done a little smoother, and so I hope this is something we won't encounter again any time soon. With that said I do think that because this is a shorter book than many of her others and because she wants each series to be a potential entry point I understood the need for it and it wasn't a major detraction at all for me.<br /><br />The ending of this book is not what I was expecting at all. I think it's rather abrupt and very 'stop you in your tracks'. I just didn't see it heading that way, and I didn't think that it would be so sudden and wild. I think it worked as a shock factor and it was pretty bold and daring to end a book that way, it certainly makes me want to know what will happen next and I can't wait to move on with the story. A solid 4* read overall, and of course one I really enjoyed!<br /><br />(I read this as part of the #BookBuddyAThon with Mercedes)</span>
  <a data-text-id="12811059923801634055" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2828331316" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2828331316" />
    <a title="Ron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43881851-ron"><img alt="Ron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557265090p2/43881851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2828331316?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ron" href="/user/show/43881851-ron">Ron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780061561658" href="/book/show/8182150-dragon-keeper">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43881851-ron?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43881851-ron?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2828331316" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11984393752456020936">Three years ago, after reading the book one of the Fitz and the Fool series (Hobb's finale that somehow left me both content and wanting more – Will there be more beyond that end? I continue to hope.), I had decided to fill in the gaps left open by reading The Liveship Traders Trilogy and this quartet of books called The Rain Wilds Chronicles. Well, I succeeded in only part of that goal by finishing the Liveship books, before being drawn back to Fitz's final plight. I'm not alone in doing so. I'</span>
  <span id="freeText11984393752456020936" style="display:none">Three years ago, after reading the book one of the Fitz and the Fool series (Hobb's finale that somehow left me both content and wanting more – Will there be more beyond that end? I continue to hope.), I had decided to fill in the gaps left open by reading The Liveship Traders Trilogy and this quartet of books called The Rain Wilds Chronicles. Well, I succeeded in only part of that goal by finishing the Liveship books, before being drawn back to Fitz's final plight. I'm not alone in doing so. I've seen many online ask the question (even to Hobb herself) of whether reading all of the trilogies are necessary. A lot of people say yes, some say no. By the way, Hobb's answer is “yes, do read them all”. I don't think she's the kind of author just saying that to get people to read all of her works either. The further I delve into this fantasy world she has created, the more I understand the richness of one very large story broken apart only by location and character. I knew when the Fitz and the Fool arrived in Kelsingra in book 3 of the last trilogy, that I'd missed something there. I also knew the answer to it lay in this series.<br /><br />This is hardly a review of Dragon Haven, but let me tell you, I am liking the start to this series. Turns out going back to fill in the gaps has some good benefits to it. In a way, I'm seeing the past and the future of this world at the same time. That's cool. By the way, this first book has no resolution. It was certainly not meant to be a stand-alone. I know the story of these dragons and their keepers continues in book #2, and I'll be heading there, happily so.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11984393752456020936" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_143947333" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/143947333" />
    <a title="Kat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4878104-kat"><img alt="Kat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515345527p2/4878104.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/143947333?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat" href="/user/show/4878104-kat">Kat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007342594" href="/book/show/7633424-the-dragon-keeper">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4878104-kat?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer143947333" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2637328800025129984"><i>The Dragon Keeper</i> is not epic. It doesn't wow me. It doesn't overwhelm me the way Hobb's books usually do (*cough* with the exception of her <i>Soldier Son</i> trilogy, I awkwardly bit the dust halfway through it *cough*). This book should be read as an introduction to the books to come. Toward the end, things do heat up when all those newly introduced characters are thrown on a boat together (which results in the first sneaky power games) and head for a vaguely remembered magical city somewhere out th</span>
  <span id="freeText2637328800025129984" style="display:none"><i>The Dragon Keeper</i> is not epic. It doesn't wow me. It doesn't overwhelm me the way Hobb's books usually do (*cough* with the exception of her <i>Soldier Son</i> trilogy, I awkwardly bit the dust halfway through it *cough*). This book should be read as an introduction to the books to come. Toward the end, things do heat up when all those newly introduced characters are thrown on a boat together (which results in the first sneaky power games) and head for a vaguely remembered magical city somewhere out there in the Rainwilds.<br /><br />I'm super confident that the books to come will be <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/143947339" rel="nofollow noopener">amazing</a>. And I'm excited to find out what Hobb has in store. However, several of what I consider those special, superb Hobb-ingredients are missing in <i>The Dragon Keeper</i>. Compelling characters for instance. For a big chunk of the book only Alise seems nicely fleshed out. And even she lacks the spunk of Althea and Malta, the two incredible heroines from <i>The Liveship Traders</i>. Greft (a Draco Malfoy including servants) and Sedric have potential. But captain Leftrin isn't exactly Brashen Trell material. His ability to impress me in the books to come will probably co-depend on whether he's capable of successfully corrupting Alise.<br /><br />My main concern however..I miss that charming, evil bastard of a pirate Kennit!<br /> <br />Or ANY Kennit-ish character. Darn it!<br /><br />More importantly, Hobb always made a point of cleverly weaving multiple layers through her stories, some so hidden and secret, that as a reader I often sensed there was a delicious magical undercurrent to the story that was just.. beyond.. my.. reach. In <i>The Dragon Keeper</i>, what you see is mostly what you get: dragon as well as human misfits heading on a desperate dragon dung and mud filled quest. Those intriguing Rainwild people are no longer a mystery, as they were when a veiled Reyn Khuprus offered Malta the most magical gifts. The dreamlike Elderlings with their buried cities lost a little of their appeal as well, now that it has become clear that humans can become them, when touched by dragons. <br /> <br />Last but not least, is it crucial to read <i>The Liveship Traders</i> and <i>The Farseer</i> books before picking up this one? Yes and no. The latter will definitely provide you with the complete picture (and Hobb masterly connects her works, which often results in "oh my god, Amber is actually.... and wait a minute..Paragon looks exactly like... eureka moments, that I know I wouldn't have wanted to miss). But the <i>Farseer</i> books are skippable. <br />However, <i> The Dragon Keeper</i> picks up where <i>The Liveship Traders</i> trilogy left of. without having read those, I doubt this one will be a satisfying read.<br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2637328800025129984" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9595345-lisa?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9595345-lisa?shelf=backlist-burndown">backlist-burndown</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1091210986" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10076851295918742538">Review from Tenacious Reader: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.tenaciousreader.com/2015/11/27/backlist-burndown-review-dragon-keeper-by-robin-hobb/'>http://www.tenaciousreader.com/2015/1...</a><br/><br/>It took me a while to get to this series, and I’m not entirely sure why since I count Robin Hobb as one of my favorite authors. I also have to confess to reading the different series that make up The Realm of the Elderlings in the wrong order as I was ignorant of how much interconnection there is between all of them. So, lesson learned. Going into this series (The Rain Wilds Chronicles), I have read all the other published boo</span>
  <span id="freeText10076851295918742538" style="display:none">Review from Tenacious Reader: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.tenaciousreader.com/2015/11/27/backlist-burndown-review-dragon-keeper-by-robin-hobb/">http://www.tenaciousreader.com/2015/1...</a><br /><br />It took me a while to get to this series, and I’m not entirely sure why since I count Robin Hobb as one of my favorite authors. I also have to confess to reading the different series that make up The Realm of the Elderlings in the wrong order as I was ignorant of how much interconnection there is between all of them. So, lesson learned. Going into this series (The Rain Wilds Chronicles), I have read all the other published books that make up Realm of the Elderlings (for those unfamiliar, it is comprised of The Farseer Trilogy, The Liveship Traders Trilogy, The Rain Wilds Chronicles and The Fitz and the Fool Trilogy). That means I have read books both preceding and following this trilogy. I will be very upfront, reading the books/series out of order is a mistake. I really had no idea how much connected between them. But now I do, and even with my unique reading order, I am really enjoying this. Actually, I have to confess to enjoying knowing some of the connections that come from my knowledge of The Fitz and the Fool books, but I would have preferred to have read them in order and made the connections as they were presented.<br /><br />This book starts with the hatching of the cocoons created by the serpents at the end of The Liveship Traders. These poor things were not given the proper start at life as they should have been. The journey they made to cocoon was far from ideal and took its price. And as a result, the hatched dragons are sorry things that dependent on humans and confined by their lack of flight. It is an interesting situation as dragons are born with memories of their ancestors, so they are very aware of the shortcomings and the life they are missing.<br /><br />We get a much closer look at life in the Rain Wilds and what it is like to grow up “heavily touched” by the Rain Wilds. This is an area that we have seen bits of in Liveship Traders, but it was never focused on to the extent it is here. While most people in the Rain Wilds are “touched” in some way (meaning they have physical characteristics that resemble dragon traits), there are those that go beyond just the bit of scaling that many have. Thymara is a protagonist who is one of those that even by Rain Wilds standards is considered an outcast by her level of change. It’s hard not to like Thymara and her relationship with her father is touching. I also really respected her desire to do more than her father expected of her, to look for something to do with her life.<br /><br />Alise is a character that I have had a bumpier ride with. Don’t get me wrong, I like her, but there are some aspects of her personality that could make cringe at times. She is the daughter of a Bingtown trader family, but hers is not a wealthy family, and she is not terribly attractive. As she passed prime marrying age without a single suitor, she has resigned to a life of spinsterhood, until suddenly she has, for some reason, caught the eye of Hest Finback, a wealty and very handsome Trader son. Of course, as we all know, if something seems too good to be true, there is liable to be a reason. It’s just a matter of if Alise can ever truly see that reason. But even if she does, she may see the business logic in not being alone the rest of her life. She can be terribly practical. While she was anticipating spending her days alone as a spinster, she decided to take up an unusual hobby as a women, and pursue studying dragons and Elderlings. This is the part of her personality I like, her drive to do something other than just sit and embroider, and plan party and decorate. You know, all the expected hobbies of a “proper” young woman. (boring!) Alise broke from the mold by pursuing her own interests, and I had to admire her for that trait.<br /><br />I loved the intersection of the Rain Wilds characters and Alise’s storyline, bringing Bingtown and Rain Wilds together. I enjoyed seeing appearances and hearing references to characters I grew to love from Hobb’s other books and am so glad I finally am filling in this gap in my reading. Books like this reinforce my decision to do a Backlist Burndown. Dragon Keeper is the start of a journey that is making me binge read this series. So, yeah. I am glad I finally made time for this one!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10076851295918742538" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12240786872729461082">I'm glad to revisit the fantasy world created by Robin Hobb---one of the few true queens of fantasy not the fake ones---again and this journey takes us to the mysterious Rain Wild River and its forest, we travel upriver together with a bunch of Rain Wild misfits and a pack of deformed dragons in hope to discover the long-lost mystical city of dragons and the Elderlings. <br/><br/>There hadn't been any dragon walking this world for centuries and neither the dragons and the humans know what to do with each </span>
  <span id="freeText12240786872729461082" style="display:none">I'm glad to revisit the fantasy world created by Robin Hobb---one of the few true queens of fantasy not the fake ones---again and this journey takes us to the mysterious Rain Wild River and its forest, we travel upriver together with a bunch of Rain Wild misfits and a pack of deformed dragons in hope to discover the long-lost mystical city of dragons and the Elderlings. <br /><br />There hadn't been any dragon walking this world for centuries and neither the dragons and the humans know what to do with each other, so how will this pack of deformed dragons (barely fit enough to feed themselves and unable to fly like the fully-formed dragons) and their inexperienced keepers survive in the harsh wilderness of the Rain Wild?<br /><br />I'm also surprised to find despite the lack of epic battle scenes and the slow pacing, still Hobb's fantasy world is so rich and the characters and their internal struggles so real that I became engaged with them so very quickly. I'm jumping to read the second book now.<br /><br />Also, I would admit some of the characters aren't particularly likable yet Ms. Hobb still managed to show the different sides of their personalities and motives; for that I'm more than glad!<br /><br />PS: words of advice: you would be better off finish reading Hobb's <i>Liveship Traders Trilogy</i> before you start this <i>Rain Wild Chronicles</i>.<br /><br /><u>Edited@19/04/2019:</u><br /><br />I had re-read the book in Chinese and damn! After I finished I just can't wait to read the second book!</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16020552538425547158">I was looking for a great fantasy story and that is exactly what I got. This book contains dragons, and even though this is clearly the beginning of a big journey and we don't get to spend that much time with the dragons, I can sense that Robin Hobb is going to rectify that in the next books in the series. I liked how the dragons were portrayed as vulnerable as well as strong and fierce animals, because that made me grow to like them and care for them. We also get to follow the story from one of</span>
  <span id="freeText16020552538425547158" style="display:none">I was looking for a great fantasy story and that is exactly what I got. This book contains dragons, and even though this is clearly the beginning of a big journey and we don't get to spend that much time with the dragons, I can sense that Robin Hobb is going to rectify that in the next books in the series. I liked how the dragons were portrayed as vulnerable as well as strong and fierce animals, because that made me grow to like them and care for them. We also get to follow the story from one of the dragons' perspective which I thought was great. <br />Basically, this book is written in a lot of perspectives and I was a fan. I think Alise was my favourite character because she grows to be very independent, but there was not one character that I didn't like reading about. I was a bit confused, though, with the letters appearing between each chapter. They didn't add anything to the story for me, and I read through them quickly so that I could get on with the real story. <br />All in all, I was quite a fan of this book and that's why I immediately ordered the sequel so that I can continue on with the journey.</span>

It could have easily been half as it is now and would have been almost perfect. <div id="review_63290246" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/63290246" />
    <a title="Jackie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/221770-jackie"><img alt="Jackie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442462335p2/221770.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1971784895" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7574532255828746297">If I did't already have Robin Hobb in my blood I may not have loved this book. As it is, I do and I did. <br/><br/>This is the continuation of the dragon's story that started in Live Ships. When I read Live Ships, the bit about the dragons was my least favourite part so I wasn't sure how much I would like Rain Wilds. Tintaglia kind of irritates me. <br/><br/>Turns out, it was great to return to the Rain Wilds. And there are some amazing new characters and relationships to get sucked in to. It's a bit of a slow star</span>
  <span id="freeText7574532255828746297" style="display:none">If I did't already have Robin Hobb in my blood I may not have loved this book. As it is, I do and I did. <br /><br />This is the continuation of the dragon's story that started in Live Ships. When I read Live Ships, the bit about the dragons was my least favourite part so I wasn't sure how much I would like Rain Wilds. Tintaglia kind of irritates me. <br /><br />Turns out, it was great to return to the Rain Wilds. And there are some amazing new characters and relationships to get sucked in to. It's a bit of a slow start but there's just such a steady pace to Hobb's books that I didn't mind... it's almost hypnotic. <br /><br />The dragons are much more interesting that I had expected. They still have their serpent personalities that we saw in Live Ships, some are even recognizable. <br /><br />This book is clearly a beginning to a longer story. It stops abruptly and doesn't give you much choice but to keep reading on into the next instalment. I literally finished this book and started the next like it was a new chapter. I didn't plan on back to back reads but, like I said, there wasn't much choice.<br /><br />Another bonus; the audio book has the same narrator as Live Ships making it that much more familiar. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7574532255828746297" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Journeying along the Rain Wilds we see a whole new cast of characters. They are such strongly written and so individual in nature that they come alive off the page. While there are so many characters to love, there are also quite a few that I love to hate.   <span id="freeText7301382749301887548" style="display:none">It's always a pleasure to read more from the world of the Elderlings and this book was no exception. Journeying along the Rain Wilds we see a whole new cast of characters. They are such strongly written and so individual in nature that they come alive off the page. While there are so many characters to love, there are also quite a few that I love to hate. This is Robin Hobb afterall, she knows how to write those villains. <br /><br />It was also such a treat to have those little moments of meeting up with characters from past series. Those moments were so heartwarming &lt;3 <br /><br />While we are only in the beginnings of the journey of the dragons and their keepers I'm very excited to see them trek onwards. I really wanna see these misfits fight the odds and win ~</span>

<div id="review_1183934528" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1183934528" />
    <a title="Sad Sunday (If I say it&#39;s bad, it&#39;s bad)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22985424-sad-sunday-if-i-say-it-s-bad-it-s-bad"><img alt="Sad Sunday (If I say it&#39;s bad, it&#39;s bad)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544800600p2/22985424.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1183934528?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sad Sunday (If I say it&#39;s bad, it&#39;s bad)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sad Sunday (If I say it&#39;s bad, it&#39;s bad)" href="/user/show/22985424-sad-sunday-if-i-say-it-s-bad-it-s-bad">Sad Sunday (If I say it&#39;s bad, it&#39;s bad)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1183934528" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17806240094149999207"><i>I like dragons!</i> (DNFs <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19549841.Seraphina__Seraphina___1_' title='Seraphina (Seraphina, #1) by Rachel Hartman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Seraphina</a>)<br/><i>I don't like series!</i> (Reads The Witcher saga like there is no tomorrow)<br/><i>Females in magic rock!</i> (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38619.Magic_Bites__Kate_Daniels___1_' title='Magic Bites (Kate Daniels, #1) by Ilona Andrews' rel='nofollow noopener'>Magic Bites</a> is somewhere in my attic...)<br/><i>I looooove old fashioned high fantasy!</i> (If you bring <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/140671.The_Black_Company__The_Chronicles_of_the_Black_Company___1_' title='The Black Company (The Chronicles of the Black Company, #1) by Glen Cook' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Black Company</a> close - it hisses at me)<br/><br/>So, I had doubts plunging into this book. And I think the first half is 3*. But somehow I grew to like it as I read further. Maybe it's still 3,5* but I would really like to read series further. <br/><br/>The author takes her time with everything -</span>
  <span id="freeText17806240094149999207" style="display:none"><i>I like dragons!</i> (DNFs <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19549841.Seraphina__Seraphina___1_" title="Seraphina (Seraphina, #1) by Rachel Hartman" rel="nofollow noopener">Seraphina</a>)<br><i>I don't like series!</i> (Reads The Witcher saga like there is no tomorrow)<br><i>Females in magic rock!</i> (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38619.Magic_Bites__Kate_Daniels___1_" title="Magic Bites (Kate Daniels, #1) by Ilona Andrews" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Bites</a> is somewhere in my attic...)<br><i>I looooove old fashioned high fantasy!</i> (If you bring <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/140671.The_Black_Company__The_Chronicles_of_the_Black_Company___1_" title="The Black Company (The Chronicles of the Black Company, #1) by Glen Cook" rel="nofollow noopener">The Black Company</a> close - it hisses at me)<br><br>So, I had doubts plunging into this book. And I think the first half is 3*. But somehow I grew to like it as I read further. Maybe it's still 3,5* but I would really like to read series further. <br><br>The author takes her time with everything - there is plenty of narratives while not much is happening. But I like how Hobb manages to jump from one character to another - you can't almost feel the "jump" but the characters still seem alive and different. But well, there is plenty of narratives and sometimes I wanted to scream "Move faster!" and push the pedal to the floor. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467977866ra/19652317.gif" width="350" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>The aspect of ancient civilization is greatly expanded. Somehow I felt like all this could have happened in ancient Mesopotamia or some old jungle area. I think the author did a good job of building a lush environment, even if it reminds me of the jungle, it still had a twist. I think unique world-building helps the story a lot. <br><br>Well, if the story was a little slow, I have no "-" signs to hang on the characters. If one was an asshole, he was an asshole to the very max. Of course, I am always rooting for the good guys (ummm, well sometimes I change sides) and I want badies to be properly punished, but in The Dragon Keeper villains were well written and believable - they had their reasons and motives. The group of keepers reminded me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7624.Lord_of_the_Flies" title="Lord of the Flies by William Golding" rel="nofollow noopener">Lord of the Flies</a> but that is also the reason I would love to know more - how everything will turn out. And of course, I am keeping my fingers crossed for a positive romance outcome (sheesh, that sound yuck).<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509905354ra/24369630.gif" width="350" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="17806240094149999207" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer460567859" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5459966497900319528"><b>Executive Summary:</b> This one may only be for big Robin Hobb fans, and those who didn't read/like Liveship Traders need not apply.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br/>I tore through the first 9 books of Ms. Hobb's Ederlings world last year. This series wasn't complete however so I wasn't in a rush to start it.<br/><br/>After almost a year away, it's good to be back. There is some overlap with the events of Tawny man, so I'd recommend you have read those as well as Liveship before tackling this one.<br/><br/>That said this book is slow. An</span>
  <span id="freeText5459966497900319528" style="display:none"><b>Executive Summary:</b> This one may only be for big Robin Hobb fans, and those who didn't read/like Liveship Traders need not apply.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br />I tore through the first 9 books of Ms. Hobb's Ederlings world last year. This series wasn't complete however so I wasn't in a rush to start it.<br /><br />After almost a year away, it's good to be back. There is some overlap with the events of Tawny man, so I'd recommend you have read those as well as Liveship before tackling this one.<br /><br />That said this book is slow. Any fan of Ms. Hobb will be used to this by now. She tends to meander at the start of her stories and takes her time before the main plot begins. This book might be the worst of the bunch. If that aspect of her writing bothers you, this series may not be for you.<br /><br />I think in any other author I might give up in frustration, but for me Ms. Hobb's writing is such that I seem to enjoy myself even if very little action is taking place. I can't really put my finger on why either. Maybe she's skilled me or something..<br /><br />Things do finally get going however and we're introduced several new characters along the way that we know pretty well by the time they do. For fans of Liveship there are some appearances by old friends, who make me smile and cheer when they showed up however briefly.<br /><br />I think this is where Ms. Hobb shines best. I've rarely love or despise characters as much as I tend to with hers. This series adds a few new ones that I may come to love, and certainly has several that I already can't stand.<br /><br />My only real complaint here is that the book sort of stops rather than ends. Just as things are really getting good too. I really just want to jump right into <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7011403.Dragon_Haven__Rain_Wild_Chronicles___2_" title="Dragon Haven (Rain Wild Chronicles, #2) by Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragon Haven</a>, which thankfully I can do if I want to, but if I had to wait, or if you didn't want to read the whole series at once, could be annoying.<br /><br />I think Ms. Hobb's done a much better with ending her other early books in a series than this. That said I'm eager to continue on and see where things go from here now that the stage has been set.<br /><br />3.5 Stars rounded up because I love Ms. Hobb.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5459966497900319528" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1405972503" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1405972503" />
    <a title="Pam Baddeley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42764850-pam-baddeley"><img alt="Pam Baddeley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442488147p2/42764850.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1405972503?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pam Baddeley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pam Baddeley" href="/user/show/42764850-pam-baddeley">Pam Baddeley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42764850-pam-baddeley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1405972503" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1467641944069364431">The first volume of the series opens as queen dragon Tintaglia assists the sea serpents who have made the hard journey up the Rain Wilds river to the muddy beach at Cassarick, one of the tree-house settlements near to a buried city of the long-vanished Elderlings, to complete the cocoons in which they will metamorphose into dragons. Sisarqua, one of the serpents from the earlier Liveships trilogy, is the viewpoint character for scenes from the dragon aspect.<br/><br/>The overlong time spent as serpents, b</span>
  <span id="freeText1467641944069364431" style="display:none">The first volume of the series opens as queen dragon Tintaglia assists the sea serpents who have made the hard journey up the Rain Wilds river to the muddy beach at Cassarick, one of the tree-house settlements near to a buried city of the long-vanished Elderlings, to complete the cocoons in which they will metamorphose into dragons. Sisarqua, one of the serpents from the earlier Liveships trilogy, is the viewpoint character for scenes from the dragon aspect.<br /><br />The overlong time spent as serpents, because of the human genocide of the dragon race - their cocoons were cut up and turned into liveships and other artefacts and the fetal dragons were killed - plus the changed condition of the river and its surroundings, and their own undernourished state, are all factors that contribute to the attrition rate among the serpents. Only a small number finally hatch as dragons and are misshapen and weak, unable to fly and vastly disappointing the humans who had anticipated a better 'return' for their assistance.<br /><br />By this time, the queen dragon Tintaglia has been gone for some time, accompanying Icefyre, the black dragon released from the ice in a connected Fitz-focused trilogy, and so the burden of caring for the infant dragons falls onto the human community which becomes increasingly reluctant to hunt for them and provide the meat they need, and leaves them in squalid, parasite-ridden conditions. Eventually the Traders in charge decide the best solution is to recruit orphans and other misfits who have been 'Touched' by the Rain Wilds and have scales and other features which make them second class citizens. These young people are to become dragon keepers, and are sent off upriver to find somewhere the dragons can settle, accompanied by a liveship barge, Tarman, and his crew, led by Captain Leftrin.<br /><br />One of the main aspects of the book therefore, is the development of relationships between the youngsters, and the stresses among them. Girls are in the minority, and some of the boys, led by an unpleasant individual called Greft, insist that they "choose" a mate. The viewpoint keeper, Thymara, who was saved by her father from being exposed in the forest and killed, resists this, despite it putting strain on her old friendship with one of their number, Tats, the sole keeper who is not Touched, but is instead the son of an ex-slave and one of the Tatooed ex-slave community, also outsiders.<br /><br />Other threads interweave into the narrative such as the story of Bingtown Trader daughter Alise, a scholar who has studied the history of the dragons and the changed humans who served them, the Elderlings. She is married to a handsome Trader heir but too late discovers his self-centred and spiteful character. Her only support is his secretary, Sedric, a childhood friend of hers. The marriage comes under increasing strain and Alise wins the chance to go up the Rain Wilds river to study the dragons for herself, though accompanied by Sedric who has been sent by her husband as a punishment for reasons of their own. When she discovers that the dragons are about to set off upriver, she decides to accompany them, having been hired by the local Traders Guild as a dragon expert after demonstrating some knowledge of the legendary Elderling city of Kelsingra. She becomes involved with Captain Leftrin, who has his own secret concerning recent modifications to his liveship and is being blackmailed by the Chaldeans who are desperate to get dragon parts to cure their tyrannical Duke. Sedric, meanwhile, has his own reasons for wanting to obtain dragon parts, and also takes seriously his role as chaperone to Alise.<br /><br />All this is interwoven in the narrative of the journey upriver and forms an interesting and page-turning tale. There are also a few cameos by characters who were in the earlier LiveShips trilogy such as Reyn and Malta, who were transformed into Elderlings by Tintaglia, and Althea and her husband the joint captains of Paragon, the formerly-mad Live Ship. Although the dragons are not 'real' dragons given their deficiencies, I enjoyed the fact that so much of the story is from their viewpoint as selfish, proud, arrogant and frequently angry and violent creatures. Only Mercor, who must be the former prophet serpent of the earlier books, has more of a calm and pragmatic side to his nature. I thoroughly enjoyed the book, but not quite to the extent of viewing it as a 'keeper' which I envisaged re-reading at some point, so am awarding it 4 stars.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1467641944069364431" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_765017159" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer3638856917863108430">I listened to this on Audible and really enjoyed Saskia Butler's narration - maybe not quite as much as Nick Taylor in the Tawny Man Trilogy, but she was still very easy to listen to.<br/><br/>The story picks up shortly after the events of the Liveships Trilogy and we get to see the serpents cocoon and then hatch as dragons on the shores of the Wild Rains River. Unfortunately, most of the dragons die and what remain are stunted and deformed and have to be tended by humans who see them as little more than </span>
  <span id="freeText3638856917863108430" style="display:none">I listened to this on Audible and really enjoyed Saskia Butler's narration - maybe not quite as much as Nick Taylor in the Tawny Man Trilogy, but she was still very easy to listen to.<br /><br />The story picks up shortly after the events of the Liveships Trilogy and we get to see the serpents cocoon and then hatch as dragons on the shores of the Wild Rains River. Unfortunately, most of the dragons die and what remain are stunted and deformed and have to be tended by humans who see them as little more than cattle. Having ancestral memories of what they should be only serves to cruelly torment the malformed dragons. In the absence of Tintaglia, the dragons come up with their own plan to rise above their squalor.<br /><br />The plot in this book was slow, even for Hobb, which is saying something. As usual, I just didn't care because I was too wrapped up in the lives of the characters. Again, Robin Hobb generates most of the dramatic tension from her characters rather than the plot and this book we see a cast of new characters, with cameo appearances by characters from Liveships. <br /><br />The first and second book of this series were originally written as one book but was split into two by the publishers. As such, this book kind of just ends abruptly - no cliffhanger finish, no ending climax - it's a "too be continued." That's not such a problem for me because I'm already sucked into the story and have the next book cued and ready to go. So far, I'm giving the story...<br /><br /><br />4 stars</span>
