    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1063304880" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1063304880" />
    <a title="Paul" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9146810-paul"><img alt="Paul" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581734604p2/9146810.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1063304880?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul" href="/user/show/9146810-paul">Paul</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061561627" href="/book/show/6550760-dragon-keeper">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9146810-paul?shelf=own-hardback">own-hardback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9146810-paul?shelf=z_archive17_read-2017books">z_archive17_read-2017books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9146810-paul?shelf=z_archive17_read-2017fromshelf">z_archive17_read-2017fromshelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9146810-paul?shelf=z_archive17_read-2017all">z_archive17_read-2017all</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9146810-paul?shelf=z_archive17_libraryaudio2017">z_archive17_libraryaudio2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1063304880" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11885737950981484706">I'm back into The Realm of the Elderlings and I certainly missed it. I missed Robin Hobb's slow character building and detailed scenes. Dragon Keeper focuses our attention on the Rain Wilds and a few characters from Bingtown as well. Our first character is a debutante woman, named Alise, from Bingtown with a scholarly appreciation to learn more about the dragons and Elderlings. She is in a loveless marriage with a man, Hest, that is in a relationship with his male assistant, Sedric. In exchange </span>
  <span id="freeText11885737950981484706" style="display:none">I'm back into The Realm of the Elderlings and I certainly missed it. I missed Robin Hobb's slow character building and detailed scenes. Dragon Keeper focuses our attention on the Rain Wilds and a few characters from Bingtown as well. Our first character is a debutante woman, named Alise, from Bingtown with a scholarly appreciation to learn more about the dragons and Elderlings. She is in a loveless marriage with a man, Hest, that is in a relationship with his male assistant, Sedric. In exchange for possibly giving Hest an heir, Alise is free to spend Hest's money on acquiring scrolls that detail the history of the Elderlings and Dragons. When Alise gets an opportunity to visit the newly hatched Dragons, deformed as they are, she jumps at the opportunity to journey up river along with Sedric. This part of the story really reminded me of Marie Brennan's The Memoirs of Lady Trent books.<br /><br />Our other main character is a young Rain Wilds girl named Thymara. She has claws and scaling that causes her to be on the outside of the Rain Wilds' society but she is also resourceful and a great hunter-gatherer. When the opportunity to go up the river with the Dragons to find their legendary home of Kelsingra happens, Thymara volunteers to join the dragons as a helper. When Alise gets to the launching of the party city and finds everyone is leaving with her scholarly subjects, she decides to go on this adventure with all the Rain Wild teenagers to study the Dragons. <br /><br />Like most Hobb books, this is a slow burn of a book. The details I talked about above cover the majority of the book. There are a few other characters we get points of view from but Thymara and Alise are the most important. Hobb likes to give the reader inexperienced characters that will have great character growth through a series and I must admit that these characters are in a great position to have some specular growth. I cannot wait to see how the characters change and grow as we move on into this story. <br /><br />I liked this book but it is very much a setup book. A lot less happens in this book than the other Hobb first books and because of that I only gave it a 3. Even though I enjoyed it and love the characters, for the most part, the book is uneventful. I read this in the physical book and on audiobook and I was happy to do so. I think the audiobook made the slow parts a lot more engaging. So my recommendation is to check your library app and see if this is available and listen to some/read some. <br /><br />Super happy to be back reading Hobbs books and looking forward to the next three books in this series.<br /><br /><b>3/5<br />13/25 Possible Score<br />3 - Plot<br />3 - Characters<br />2 - World Building <br />3 - Writing Style<br />2 - Heart and Mind Aspect</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="11885737950981484706" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1914220755?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle Morrell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle Morrell" href="/user/show/127000-michelle-morrell">Michelle Morrell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/127000-michelle-morrell?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/127000-michelle-morrell?shelf=x-read-2017">x-read-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1914220755" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12337999781320529423">And we begin another series. This one, taking place in Bingtown (a bit) and the Rain Wilds (mostly) is classic Hobb goodness. <br/><br/>The serpents that traveled so long and so hard in the Liveship books have completed their hibernation and are now dragons. Only, their travel was too long and too hard, only a handful have survived, and they are all stunted in one way or another. Unable to fly, dependent on the humans to feed them now that Tingtalia has disappeared, the situation is untenable. <br/><br/>Until the d</span>
  <span id="freeText12337999781320529423" style="display:none">And we begin another series. This one, taking place in Bingtown (a bit) and the Rain Wilds (mostly) is classic Hobb goodness. <br /><br />The serpents that traveled so long and so hard in the Liveship books have completed their hibernation and are now dragons. Only, their travel was too long and too hard, only a handful have survived, and they are all stunted in one way or another. Unable to fly, dependent on the humans to feed them now that Tingtalia has disappeared, the situation is untenable. <br /><br />Until the dragons come up with a plan. Convince the humans to assist them to the fabled city of Kelsingra. <br /><br />We meet the usual cast of character, but as this is one of Hobb's greatest strengths, they are all complex and delightful, dragon and human alike (even the ones I want to kick). Preparations are made and the journey ... begins?<br /><br />I read this in digital form (which I *never* do, so that tells you how much I love her books), and it just ... ended. I had to scour the internet (a whole 7 minutes of Googling) to realize that yes, it does just end like that, right in the middle of the story, just when the long exposition is finally paying off. Thankfully, I have volume 2 right here. I would not be half as amused if I had to wait for the next publication date.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12337999781320529423" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vsF5tcW0qRCxSEEX/9yInL4IgKoZ9y/odR4Nh2xBmVUOp6t83xvDLvzlKHb0J/r34WhNXobFTMz3nlenifEh2A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('76Fy9HD81B5imFFs/sawmbdgcCvHCy/AWI4ZK+DOPTVfx6A9alO+IC81OA31PcLy6AC931g5TOTaDkMLBX6FuA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/25307.Robin_Hobb">About Robin Hobb</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/25307.Robin_Hobb">Robin Hobb

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3125239538448813791">** I am shocked to find that some people think a 2 star 'I liked it' rating is a bad rating. What? I liked it. I LIKED it! That means I read the whole thing, to the last page, in spite of my life raining comets on me. It's a good book that survives the reading process with me. If a book is so-so, it ends up under the bed somewhere, or maybe under a stinky judo bag in the back of the van. So a 2 st</span>
  <span id="freeText3125239538448813791" style="display:none">** I am shocked to find that some people think a 2 star 'I liked it' rating is a bad rating. What? I liked it. I LIKED it! That means I read the whole thing, to the last page, in spite of my life raining comets on me. It's a good book that survives the reading process with me. If a book is so-so, it ends up under the bed somewhere, or maybe under a stinky judo bag in the back of the van. So a 2 star from me means,yes, I liked the book, and I'd loan it to a friend and it went everywhere in my jacket pocket or purse until I finished it. A 3 star means that I've ignored friends to finish it and my sink is full of dirty dishes. A 4 star means I'm probably in trouble with my editor for missing a deadline because I was reading this book. But I want you to know . . . I don't finish books I don't like. There's too many good ones out there waiting to be found.<br /><br /><br />Robin Hobb is the author of three well-received fantasy trilogies: The Farseer Trilogy (Assassin’s Apprentice, Royal Assassin, and Assassin’s Quest), The Liveship Traders Trilogy (Ship of Magic, Mad Ship and Ship of Destiny) and the Tawny Man Trilogy (Fool’s Errand, Golden Fool, and Fool’s Fate) Her current work in progress is entitled Shaman’s Crossing. Robin Hobb lives and works in Tacoma, Washington, and has been a professional writer for over 30 years.<br /><br />In addition to writing, her interests include gardening, mushrooming, and beachcombing. She and her husband Fred have three grown children and one teenager, and three grand-children.<br /><br />She also writes as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/53255.Megan_Lindholm" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Lindholm</a>, and works under that name have been finalists for the Hugo award, the Nebula Award, and the Endeavor award. She has twice won an Isaac Asimov’s Science Fiction Readers’ Award.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3125239538448813791" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
